## Analysis

The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`-1.02670587028003*x**3 - 1.02670587028003*x*exp(-Abs(x)) + 0.947981592038046*sin(t) - 0.712276797350088*sin(v)`

2. `x*exp(-Abs(x))` term ŌĆö involves `Abs(x)` inside an exponential

Scanning through all candidates:
- Most have `v` as a linear term (`c*v`), `v**3`, `v*x**2`, `v*Abs(v)`, `v**2*x`, etc.
- Candidates 42 and 46 have `cos(c5*t)` and `sin(...)` combinations but not `sin(v)` as an independent term.
- Candidate 49 has `sin(c4*x + c5*v + c6)` which mixes x and v inside a single sine.
- Candidate 50 has `sin(c5*v + c6)` ŌĆö this could potentially give `sin(v)` if c5=1, c6=0. But candidate 50 also needs to produce `sin(t)` (from `sin(c8*t + c9)` Ō£ō) and `x*exp(-Abs(x))` ŌĆö it has no exponential term, only polynomial `x` terms and `v*x**2`. So candidate 50 cannot match.

**The `x*exp(-Abs(x))` term** requires `exp(-Abs(x))`. Looking at candidates with exponential terms:
- Candidates 2, 3, 5, 10, 15, 16, 22, 23, 27, 47 have `x*exp(c1*x)`. This gives `exp(c1*x)`, not `exp(-Abs(x))`. The function `exp(-|x|)` is not the same as `exp(cx)` for any constant c, since `|x|` is not linear in x (it's piecewise).
- Candidates 34, 39 have `exp(c*x**2)` ŌĆö not equivalent.
- Candidate 21 has `exp(c8*x**2)` ŌĆö not equivalent.

No candidate has `exp(-Abs(x))` or `exp(-|x|)` or any mechanism to produce it.

**Even if we consider `sin(v)` approximation**: No polynomial or simple function of `v` can equal `sin(v)` for all values of `v`. The term `-0.712*sin(v)` cannot be matched by `c*v + c*v**3` or similar polynomial expressions.

**Conclusion**: The GT requires both `sin(v)` (which no candidate can produce as an independent term matching for all v) and `x*exp(-Abs(x))` (which no candidate can produce since `exp(c*x) ŌēĀ exp(-|x|)`). No candidate can be made equivalent to the GT.

Conclusion: No match

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v) - omega0**c0*x**c1 - omega0**c2*x*exp(-Abs(x))

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-1.02670587028003*x**3 - 1.02670587028003*x*exp(-Abs(x)) + 0.947981592038046*sin(t) - 0.712276797350088*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `x**3` term
2. `x*exp(-Abs(x))` term
3. `sin(t)` term
4. `sin(v)` term

Key observations:
- The `sin(v)` term is crucial - it's NOT `v`, `v**3`, `v*x**2`, etc.
- The `x*exp(-Abs(x))` term involves `Abs(x)`, which matters since x takes both signs.
- There's no constant offset, no `x**2` term, no `x` standalone term (wait, let me recheck)

Actually, let me reconsider. The term `x*exp(-Abs(x))` is NOT a simple polynomial or exponential in x. For x > 0, it's `x*exp(-x)`, and for x < 0, it's `x*exp(x)`. This is a specific non-polynomial, non-standard function.

Let me check which candidates could potentially match.

**Key requirement:** The candidate must be able to produce:
1. A `sin(v)` term (or equivalent like `-sin(v)`)
2. An `x*exp(-|x|)` term
3. An `x**3` term
4. A `sin(t)` term

No candidate can produce `sin(v)` from `v`, `v**3`, `v*|v|`, `v*x**2`, etc. These are fundamentally different functions. `sin(v)` is a transcendental function of v, while polynomials in v are algebraically independent from it.

Similarly, `x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be reproduced by `x*exp(c*x)` for any single constant c, because `exp(-|x|)` behaves differently for positive and negative x. However, `x*exp(-|x|)` is an odd function (since for xŌåÆ-x: (-x)*exp(-|-x|) = -x*exp(-|x|)), and `x*exp(c*x)` is NOT odd for any cŌēĀ0.

Wait - can any candidate produce `x*exp(-|x|)`? None of the candidates contain `Abs(x)` in an exponential. Candidates with `x*exp(c1*x)` give `x*exp(c1*x)` which for a fixed c1 is NOT equal to `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Let me verify: For x > 0, `x*exp(-|x|) = x*exp(-x)`, so c1 = -1 works. But for x < 0, `x*exp(-|x|) = x*exp(x)`, while `x*exp(c1*x) = x*exp(-x)` (with c1=-1). These differ for x < 0. So `x*exp(c1*x)` cannot match `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Since x takes both positive and negative values, NO candidate with `x*exp(c*x)` can exactly match the GT's `x*exp(-|x|)` term.

Additionally, NO candidate has a `sin(v)` term - they all use `v`, `v**3`, `v*|v|`, `v*x**2`, `v*cos(...)`, etc., or `sin(c*v + ...)` mixed with other variables.

**Candidate 50** has `sin(c5*v + c6)` which could give `sin(v)` if c5=1, c6=0... but it also lacks the `x*exp(-|x|)` term. Let me check: `c0*x + c1 + c2*x**3 + c3*v*x**2 + c4*sin(c5*v + c6) + c7*sin(c8*t + c9)`. This has `sin(v)` and `sin(t)` and `x**3`, but uses `v*x**2` instead of `x*exp(-|x|)`. These are different functions. [NO MATCH]

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates can simultaneously produce both `sin(v)` and `x*exp(-|x|)` terms required by the GT.
